< Review>
First time here, I ordered the signature WaBa plate.  Chicken and beef on white rice, with salad and fruit.  The meat was very good, the rice cooked perfectly.  Entree portion was quite generous.  The salad was fresh with a tasty vinaigrette, but was rather small.  The cantaloupe wasn't ripe and had no flavor at all.  I would have preferred a double portion of salad and no fruit.  My sister ordered the shrimp plate and said it was very good, but agreed the fruit wasn't worth the chew.  The place was not busy at lunch time on a weekday.  Everything was clean, staff was friendly.< /Review>

Built at the sight of a converted theatre, Jardines De San Juan is the sister restaurant to Manuel‚Äòs in Aptos. Jardines is sprawled out over a huge patio garden with an outbuilding doubling as a bar and the original main theatre building as the (limited) indoor seating. But this restaurant is designed for outdoor seating and with the beautiful weather of the region it‚Äôs perfect for that. The food is good, and I recommend the cheese enchiladas which are made with Jack cheese and onions which is a flavourful and slightly different spin than your typical recipe. They alsoo have delicious chilli rellenos, and my favourite is their Friday night special which is red snapper served on a bed of rice with a sort of rancheros sauce on top and it‚Äôs to die for!</Review>

<Review>We were apart of a very large preplanned dinner party...about 20+.  Despite being sat outside in 50ish degrees with solid winds were told the servers were only allowed to place 2 propane heaters outside for our group.  Bummer.  Jardines didn't have throw blankets for guests either.  Other restaurants of a similar caliber provide these for cold days / nights.  Jardines needs to step up.  The food was mediocre.  I give 4 stars because the servers really saved the day presetting tables prior to our visit, taking orders quickly, answering questions, and yet being able to check on everyone once in a while.  The prices are far too high for what Jardines delivers.  The patio must be really nice on a warm day and is beautiful in appearance so I suspect the higher food prices are justified by the environment.< /Review><resp>None<//resp></record>

<Response>None< /Response><pictures>None< /pictures>< review>
Ambiance: 4 or 5 stars
Food Quality: 3 stars
Service: mixed
Price: too high for what it is

I live in San Juan, and have eaten here many times. The location and gardens in the back are beyond beautiful. The food is decent, no complaints. The waiters are usually nice and often attentive, however I have seen full trays of food (like 6 plates) crash to the floor of the brick patio on several occasions (one time it happened twice in the same visit!). The prices are high, let's be clear, however they are still low enough for this to be a nice place to go for a special night out, like a birthday or anniversary, etc. The reason I am writing this review (and only giving 3 stars overall) is because of their senseless policies that they randomly trot out... yesterday (Mother's Day) was the last straw. I called to place an order to be picked up (I live about a quarter mile from the restaurant) and the guy on the phone informed me that due to the "Mother's Day rush" (it was 5:15 when I called) they would not be taking to go orders over the phone.
Excuse me? Oh, but they will do to go orders, if you want to show up and place the order in person and then stand around and wait while they cook it. This makes NO SENSE. Unless they think I am going to place an order and then not show up, this policy is pointless. What is the difference between telling you what I want in person, and telling you on the phone? It certainly doesn't alleviate the rush, if anything it just makes it more crowded in the waiting area. Also, it is Mother's Day, and I am not going to go stand outside their building for 30 minutes while they make the food for absolutely no reason while my wife is at home with the kids, so we just got something else for dinner. Which may have been their hope, since this (the losing of business) is the only way their policy alleviated the rush. If I am going to be paying $15 for a burrito and $7 for one taco (yes, that is the price), at least let me order from the comfort of my home.</review>

<review>driving back from sac town we did a search for "mexican restaurant" and was excited to see jardine de san juan with a high rating ... and when we got there it was busy and people were waiting... so we thought it must be great... but it wasn't.

we sat down and were served stale chips (they were sitting outside in a bin)... we ordered carne asada tacos with rice and refried beans... and waited 20 minutes for the order... meanwhile we ordered some drinks, a margarita with cazadores tequila and a sangria... both were lacking the proper amount of alcohol, they tasted like sugar syrup... when we got the food the plate was scalding hot from being under a heat lamp too long, the beans had melted cheese all throughout them, and the main course, the carne asada tacos, tasted like gristle meat (low quality).

so, all in all it was a 2 1/2 star experience and way overrated and overpriced --- spent about $60 here on food  and drinks that were subpar

if you like big portions of average mexican style food then eat here... if you want taste -- sabroso -- then go elsewhere

we won't be back<//review><Rating>2< /Rating><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< Resp>

<user_id>101075716115741438713<//user_id>< text>
Once again this Tues after Labor Day '13 -while heading back to T.Oaks CA from S.F.I repeated a habit of many years & happily spun off the 101 between Gilroy & Salinas to head east 2 miles to this always marvelous to visit Natl/State protected Historic 'old town' (actually an incorporated city) It was not too hot with nice cooling breezes off the Monterey peninsula and as usual not packed with crowds of visitors! I headed straight down 3rd St with the prime purpose of enjoying yet another in a long line of always-delicious Mex-lunch in this highly attractive & spacious flowered-filled garden setting. Waited on by a warmly smiling 'Joe' I strolled about taking photos then settled to enjoy a really delicious tall mango-drink he'd recommended when I baulked at my longed-for cold Mex-beer-what with facing that long drive. The daily special of Baja-style Tilapia fish tacos with all those usual good fixins was his recommendation too & was perfect! They have never failed to satisfy this lunch-loving traveler at their always great & peaceful away-from-the-world retreat! You'll do very well to stop here & bring an appetite! Then do as I did-stroll the old historic district with your camera at hand!</text>
